SASL authentication implementation is structured around a central server authenticator that manages the entire authentication lifecycle. The key components are:\\n\\n1. **Server Authenticator Core**: SaslServerAuthenticator (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java) implements the Authenticator interface and manages the overall authentication state machine. It handles the SASL handshake protocol, mechanism negotiation, and delegates to mechanism-specific SaslServer implementations. The createSaslServer() method selects the appropriate mechanism implementation based on the negotiated SASL mechanism.\\n\\n2. **Authentication Context Lifecycle**: SaslAuthenticationContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java) encapsulates the authentication context during the authentication process, wrapping javax.security.sasl.SaslServer and providing security protocol, client address, and listener information.\\n\\n3. **PLAIN Mechanism**: The PLAIN mechanism is implemented through PlainSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java), which implements the javax.security.sasl.SaslServer interface. The PlainSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServerProvider.java) registers the PlainSaslServerFactory that creates PLAIN server instances. PlainServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java) handles the JAAS callbacks for credential validation using the user_<username> format from JAAS configuration.\\n\\n4. **SCRAM Mechanism**: The SCRAM mechanism implementation includes ScramSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java) with ScramSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServerProvider.java) handling both SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 variants via ScramMechanism (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java). ScramServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java) manages credential and token validation using CredentialCache, while ScramFormatter (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java) handles SCRAM message formatting and credential generation.\\n\\n5. **GSSAPI/Kerberos Mechanism**: Kerberos authentication is handled through KerberosLogin (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosLogin.java) and KerberosClientCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosClientCallbackHandler.java). Server-side GSSAPI uses Java's built-in GSSAPI provider. KerberosName (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosName.java) and KerberosShortNamer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosShortNamer.java) handle principal name mapping according to JAAS rules defined in KerberosRule (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosRule.java).\\n\\n6. **OAuthBearer Mechanism**: OAuthBearerSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java) implements OAuth 2.0 token-based authentication with OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider.java) registering the OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory.\\n\\n7. **Mechanism Selection Infrastructure**: SaslChannelBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) orchestrates the creation of server-side authentication components. It loads JAAS contexts for enabled mechanisms, creates appropriate callback handlers based on the mechanism type, and builds the authenticator. ChannelBuilders (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java) provides factory methods for creating SASL channel builders for both client and server modes.\\n\\n8. **Callback Handler Infrastructure**: SaslServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java) provides default callback handling for all SASL mechanisms, while mechanism-specific handlers (PlainServerCallbackHandler, ScramServerCallbackHandler) override behavior for their respective mechanisms. AuthenticateCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticateCallbackHandler.java) is the interface that all callback handlers must implement.\\n\\n9. **JAAS Context Management**: JaasContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java) and JaasConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasConfig.java) manage JAAS configuration loading and context creation for both static and dynamic JAAS configurations. LoginManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/LoginManager.java) manages the lifecycle of JAAS login modules.\\n\\n10. **Credential Storage**: CredentialCache (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java) provides in-memory caching of credentials for SCRAM mechanisms, supporting dynamic credential updates via broker admin operations.\\n\\nThe authentication flow begins when a client connects to a SASL listener. SaslChannelBuilder builds the server-side channel with appropriate JAAS contexts for all enabled mechanisms. SaslServerAuthenticator receives the initial SASL handshake request, extracts the client's preferred mechanism, creates a SaslServer instance via the appropriate mechanism provider, and proceeds with the SASL token exchange until authentication succeeds or fails. Throughout this process, the mechanism-specific SaslServer implementations handle the cryptographic and validation logic, with callback handlers bridging to the broker's credential stores and authorization rules.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":9406,"cache_read_input_tokens":71220,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":9406},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"abc1177d-88b9-4205-bed3-f2b80f408d97","uuid":"6ef6d2bd-83d3-4960-945e-dc9a20c4d2c5"}

The key components are:\\n\\n1. **Server Authenticator Core**: SaslServerAuthenticator (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java) implements the Authenticator interface and manages the overall authentication state machine. The createSaslServer() method selects the appropriate mechanism implementation based on the negotiated SASL mechanism.\\n\\n2. **Authentication Context Lifecycle**: SaslAuthenticationContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java) encapsulates the authentication context during the authentication process, wrapping javax.security.sasl.SaslServer and providing security protocol, client address, and listener information.\\n\\n3. **PLAIN Mechanism**: The PLAIN mechanism is implemented through PlainSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java), which implements the javax.security.sasl.SaslServer interface. The PlainSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServerProvider.java) registers the PlainSaslServerFactory that creates PLAIN server instances. PlainServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java) handles the JAAS callbacks for credential validation using the user_<username> format from JAAS configuration.\\n\\n4. **SCRAM Mechanism**: The SCRAM mechanism implementation includes ScramSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java) with ScramSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServerProvider.java) handling both SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 variants via ScramMechanism (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java). ScramServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java) manages credential and token validation using CredentialCache, while ScramFormatter (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java) handles SCRAM message formatting and credential generation.\\n\\n5. **GSSAPI/Kerberos Mechanism**: Kerberos authentication is handled through KerberosLogin (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosLogin.java) and KerberosClientCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosClientCallbackHandler.java). Server-side GSSAPI uses Java's built-in GSSAPI provider. KerberosName (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosName.java) and KerberosShortNamer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosShortNamer.java) handle principal name mapping according to JAAS rules defined in KerberosRule (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosRule.java).\\n\\n6. **OAuthBearer Mechanism**: OAuthBearerSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java) implements OAuth 2.0 token-based authentication with OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider.java) registering the OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory.\\n\\n7. **Mechanism Selection Infrastructure**: SaslChannelBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) orchestrates the creation of server-side authentication components. It loads JAAS contexts for enabled mechanisms, creates appropriate callback handlers based on the mechanism type, and builds the authenticator. ChannelBuilders (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java) provides factory methods for creating SASL channel builders for both client and server modes.\\n\\n8. **Callback Handler Infrastructure**: SaslServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java) provides default callback handling for all SASL mechanisms, while mechanism-specific handlers (PlainServerCallbackHandler, ScramServerCallbackHandler) override behavior for their respective mechanisms. AuthenticateCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticateCallbackHandler.java) is the interface that all callback handlers must implement.\\n\\n9. **JAAS Context Management**: JaasContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java) and JaasConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasConfig.java) manage JAAS configuration loading and context creation for both static and dynamic JAAS configurations. LoginManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/LoginManager.java) manages the lifecycle of JAAS login modules.\\n\\n10. **Credential Storage**: CredentialCache (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java) provides in-memory caching of credentials for SCRAM mechanisms, supporting dynamic credential updates via broker admin operations.\\n\\nThe authentication flow begins when a client connects to a SASL listener. SaslChannelBuilder builds the server-side channel with appropriate JAAS contexts for all enabled mechanisms. SaslServerAuthenticator receives the initial SASL handshake request, extracts the client's preferred mechanism, creates a SaslServer instance via the appropriate mechanism provider, and proceeds with the SASL token exchange until authentication succeeds or fails. Throughout this process, the mechanism-specific SaslServer implementations handle the cryptographic and validation logic, with callback handlers bridging to the broker's credential stores and authorization rules.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
